				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Delta_Air_Lines_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Delta Air Lines Inc.">Delta Air Lines Inc.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Delta Air Lines, Inc.</b>, typically referred to as <b>Delta</b>, is one of the <a href="/wiki/Major_airlines_of_the_United_States" title="Major airlines of the United States">major airlines of the United States</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Legacy_carrier" title="Legacy carrier">legacy carrier</a>. It is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The airline, along with its subsidiaries and regional affiliates, including <a href="/wiki/Delta_Connection" title="Delta Connection">Delta Connection</a>, operates over 5,400 flights daily and serves 325 destinations in 52 countries on six continents.<sup id="cite_ref-statsfacts_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsfacts-12">[12]</a></sup> Delta is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-statsfacts_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsfacts-12">[12]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Delta Air Lines, Inc.</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Delta_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="Delta logo.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Delta_logo.svg/270px-Delta_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="270" height="42" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Delta_logo.svg/405px-Delta_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Delta_logo.svg/540px-Delta_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="79"></a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">

srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>4.767 billion <small>(2019)</small><sup id="cite_ref-Results2019_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Results2019-8">[8]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Asset" title="Asset">Total assets</a></th><td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>64.529 billion <small>(2019)</small><sup id="cite_ref-Results2019_8-3" rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.delta.com/">www<wbr></wbr>.delta<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: lightgrey;">Notes</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="text-align: left;">
<sup id="cite_ref-10K_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-9">[9]</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Delta has nine hubs, with <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Atlanta</a> being its largest in terms of total passengers and number of departures.<sup id="cite_ref-statsfacts_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsfacts-12">[12]</a></sup> It is ranked second among the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_largest_airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="World's largest airlines">world's largest airlines</a> by number of scheduled passengers carried, revenue passenger-kilometers flown, and fleet size. It is ranked 69th on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Delta_Air_Lines" title="History of Delta Air Lines">History of Delta Air Lines</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<p>Delta Air Lines' history begins with the world's first aerial <a href="/wiki/Crop_dusting" class="mw-redirect" title="Crop dusting">crop dusting</a> operation called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Huff_Daland_Dusters,_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Huff Daland Dusters, Inc. (page does not exist)">Huff Daland Dusters, Inc.</a> The company was founded on March 2, 1925, in <a href="/wiki/Macon,_Georgia" title="Macon, Georgia">Macon, Georgia</a>, and moved to <a href="/wiki/Monroe,_Louisiana" title="Monroe, Louisiana">Monroe, Louisiana</a>, in summer 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-Founding_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Founding-14">[14]</a></sup> They flew a Huff-Daland Duster, the first true crop duster, designed to combat the <a href="/wiki/Boll_weevil" title="Boll weevil">boll weevil</a> infestation of cotton crops.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Collett_E._Woolman" title="Collett E. Woolman">C.E. Woolman</a>, general manager and later Delta's first CEO, led a group of local investors to acquire the company's assets. Delta Air Service was incorporated on December 3, 1928, and named after the Mississippi Delta region.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-journey_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journey-1">[1]</a></sup></p><p>Passenger operations began on June 17, 1929, from Dallas, Texas, to Jackson, Mississippi, with stops at Shreveport and Monroe, Louisiana. By June 1930, service had extended east to Atlanta and west to Fort Worth, Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-First_Flights_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_Flights-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>Passenger service ceased in October 1930 when the air mail contract for the route Delta had pioneered was awarded to another airline, which purchased the assets of Delta Air Service. Local banker Travis Oliver, acting as trustee, C.E. Woolman and other local investors purchased back the crop-dusting assets of Delta Air Service and incorporated as Delta Air Corporation on December 31, 1930.
</p><p>Delta Air Corporation secured an air mail contract in 1934, and began doing business as Delta Air Lines over Mail Route 24, stretching from Fort Worth, Texas, to Charleston, South Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-First_Flights_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_Flights-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Founding_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Founding-14">[14]</a></sup></p><p>Delta moved its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Monroe,_Louisiana" title="Monroe, Louisiana">Monroe, Louisiana</a>, to its current location in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The company name officially became Delta Air Lines in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1946, the company commenced regularly scheduled <a href="/wiki/Freight_transport" title="Freight transport">freight transport</a>. In 1949, the company launched the first discounted fares between <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>. In 1953, the company launched its first international routes after the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Chicago_and_Southern_Air_Lines" title="Chicago and Southern Air Lines">Chicago and Southern Air Lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1959, it was the first airline to fly the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-8" title="Douglas DC-8">Douglas DC-8</a>. In 1960, it was the first airline to fly <a href="/wiki/Convair_880" title="Convair 880">Convair 880</a> jets. In 1964, it launched the Deltamatic reservation systems using computers in the <a href="/wiki/IBM_7070" title="IBM 7070">IBM 7070</a> series. In 1965, Delta was the first airline to fly the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-9" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-9">McDonnell Douglas DC-9</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_and_acquisitions">Growth and acquisitions</span></h3>
<p>By 1970, Delta had an all-jet fleet, and in 1972 it acquired <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Airlines" title="Northeast Airlines">Northeast Airlines</a>. Trans-Atlantic service began in 1978 with the first nonstop flights from Atlanta to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. In 1981, Delta launched a <a href="/wiki/Frequent-flyer_program" title="Frequent-flyer program">frequent-flyer program</a>. In 1987, it acquired <a href="/wiki/Western_Airlines" title="Western Airlines">Western Airlines</a>, and that same year Delta began trans-Pacific service (Atlanta-Portland, Oregon-Tokyo). In 1990, Delta was the first airline in the United States to fly <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">McDonnell Douglas MD-11</a> jets. In 1991, it acquired substantially all of <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan Am</a>'s trans-Atlantic routes and the Pan Am Shuttle, rebranded as the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Shuttle" title="Delta Shuttle">Delta Shuttle</a>. Delta was now the leading airline across the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-journey_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journey-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>In 1997, Delta was the first airline to board more than 100 million passengers in a calendar year. Also that year, Delta began an expansion of their international routes into <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p><p>In 2003, the company launched <a href="/wiki/Song_(airline)" title="Song (airline)">Song</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-journey_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journey-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Bankruptcy_and_restructuring_.282005-2007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bankruptcy_and_restructuring_(2005-2007)">Bankruptcy and restructuring (2005-2007)</span></h3>
<p>On September 14, 2005, the company filed for <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a>, citing rising fuel costs.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> It emerged from bankruptcy in April 2007 after fending off a <a href="/wiki/Hostile_takeover" class="mw-redirect" title="Hostile takeover">hostile takeover</a> from <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a> and its shares were re-listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Acquisition_of_Northwest_Airlines_.282008.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_of_Northwest_Airlines_(2008)">Acquisition of Northwest Airlines (2008)</span></h3>
<p>The acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a> was announced April 14, 2008. It was approved and consummated on October 29, 2008. Northwest continued to operate as a wholly owned subsidiary of Delta until December 31, 2009, when the Northwest Airlines operating certificate was merged into that of Delta.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Delta completed integration with Northwest on January 31, 2010, when their <a href="/wiki/Computer_reservations_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer reservations system">computer reservations system</a> and websites were combined, and the Northwest Airlines brand was officially retired.<sup id="cite_ref-mouawad_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mouawad-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations_and_hubs">Destinations and hubs</span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Delta_Air_Lines_destinations" title="List of Delta Air Lines destinations">List of Delta Air Lines destinations</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Delta_Connection_destinations" title="List of Delta Connection destinations">List of Delta Connection destinations</a></div>
<p>Delta and its worldwide alliance partners operate more than 15,000 flights per day.<sup id="cite_ref-statsfacts_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsfacts-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>Delta is the only U.S. carrier that flies to <a href="/wiki/Kotoka_International_Airport" title="Kotoka International Airport">Accra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Diagne_International_Airport" title="Blaise Diagne International Airport">Dakar</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/OR_Tambo_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="OR Tambo International Airport">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murtala_Muhammed_International_Airport" title="Murtala Muhammed International Airport">Lagos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nice_Cote_d%27Azur_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Nice Cote d'Azur Airport">Nice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Airport" title="Stuttgart Airport">Stuttgart</a>.
</p><p>In March 2020, Delta announced they are suspending all flights to continental Europe for 30 days, and cutting 40% of their capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hubs">Hubs</span></h3>
<p>Delta currently has nine hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-statsfacts_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsfacts-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Atlanta</a> – Delta's hub for the Southeast and its main gateway to Latin America and the Caribbean. In addition to its corporate headquarters, Delta operates its primary hub in Atlanta as well as <a href="/wiki/Delta_TechOps" title="Delta TechOps">Delta TechOps</a>, which is Delta's primary maintenance base.<sup id="cite_ref-ATLlargestHub_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATLlargestHub-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> – Delta's secondary transatlantic hub. Boston-Logan had previously been a Delta hub from the latter half of the 20th century to the early 2000s. The present Terminal A was built for Delta's sole use, but following the 2005 bankruptcy, Delta scaled back operations and leased 11 gates in the terminal. Delta subsequently regained all the Terminal A gates and began building up operations again in the mid 2010s, culminating in the reestablishing of BOS as a hub in 2019.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Detroit_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Detroit Metropolitan Airport">Detroit</a> – Inherited through the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines-Northwest_Airlines_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Delta Air Lines-Northwest Airlines merger">merger with Northwest</a>, Detroit serves as one of Delta's two Midwest hubs and is Delta's second largest overall. It is the primary Asian gateway for the Eastern United States and it also provides service to many destinations in the Americas and Europe.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a> – Delta's secondary West Coast hub. Delta inherited its LAX hub from <a href="/wiki/Western_Airlines" title="Western Airlines">Western Airlines</a>, but dismantled it in the mid-1990s, opting to relocate most of those aircraft to the east coast. Since then, it has re-opened the hub, offering service to select cities in Latin America, Asia, Australia and Europe, as well as major domestic cities and West Coast regional destinations.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93Saint_Paul_International_Airport" title="Minneapolis–Saint Paul International Airport">Minneapolis–Saint Paul</a> – Inherited through the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines-Northwest_Airlines_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Delta Air Lines-Northwest Airlines merger">merger with Northwest</a>, Minneapolis–Saint Paul serves as one of Delta's two Midwest hubs and is Delta's third largest overall. It is the primary Canadian gateway for the airline while also including many American metropolitan destinations, a number of regional destinations in the upper Midwest as well as some select destinations in Europe and Asia.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York–JFK</a> –  Delta's primary transatlantic hub. Delta inherited its JFK hub from its partnership with Pan Am after Pan Am's collapse in 1991. The hub also offers service on many transcontinental "prestige routes" to west coast destinations such as Los Angeles and San Francisco.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">New York–LaGuardia</a> – Delta's second New York hub. This important domestic hub was created as a result of a slot swap with the now defunct <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a>. Delta's service at LaGuardia covers numerous East Coast US cities, and a number of regional destinations in the US and Canada.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City_International_Airport" title="Salt Lake City International Airport">Salt Lake City</a> – Inherited through the <a href="/wiki/Western_Airlines" title="Western Airlines">merger with Western Airlines</a>, Salt Lake City serves as the fourth largest hub for the airline. Delta service covers most major US destinations as well as a number of regional destinations in the US, with an emphasis on the Rocky Mountain region, as well as select destinations in Canada, Mexico, and select cities in Europe and Hawaii.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seattle%E2%80%93Tacoma_International_Airport" title="Seattle–Tacoma International Airport">Seattle/Tacoma</a> – Delta's primary West Coast hub. The hub serves as an international gateway to Asia for the Western United States. Delta service also includes many major US destinations as well as regional destinations in the Pacific Northwest. Delta started aggressively building its presence in Seattle in 2011, and announced SEA's hub status in 2014, while notably sparking tensions with Seattle-based Alaska Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-airchive.com_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airchive.com-38">[38]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Alliance_and_codeshare_agreements">Alliance and codeshare agreements</span></h3>
<p>Delta was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> Alliance in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and has <a href="/wiki/Codeshare_agreement" title="Codeshare agreement">codeshare agreements</a> with the following airlines:<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 17em; -webkit-column-width: 17em; column-width: 17em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerolíneas Argentinas">Aerolíneas Argentinas</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aerom%C3%A9xico" title="Aeroméxico">Aeroméxico</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Air_Europa" title="Air Europa">Air Europa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_Airlines" title="China Airlines">China Airlines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Czech_Airlines" title="Czech Airlines">Czech Airlines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">Garuda Indonesia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gol_Transportes_A%C3%A9reos" title="Gol Transportes Aéreos">Gol Transportes Aéreos</a><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Airlines" title="Hawaiian Airlines">Hawaiian Airlines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenya_Airways" title="Kenya Airways">Kenya Airways</a><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seaborne_Airlines" title="Seaborne Airlines">Seaborne Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Transavia" title="Transavia">Transavia</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vietnam_Airlines" title="Vietnam Airlines">Vietnam Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WestJet" title="WestJet">WestJet</a><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li></ul></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_ventures">Joint ventures</span></h3>
<p>In addition to the above codeshares, Delta has also entered into joint ventures with the following airlines.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aeromexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Aeromexico">Aeromexico</a> – Delta owns 49% of Mexican <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> Aeroméxico. In 2015, Delta and Aeromexico applied for an immunized joint venture. After two years, the joint venture was approved with two conditions: both airlines had to surrender four slot pairs at <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> and 24 at <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a> to competitors (both airports have slot restrictions). The joint venture began in May 2017, at which time Aeromexico moved to Delta gates at both Kennedy and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>/<a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>/<a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> – Delta, as successor to Northwest Airlines, has a transatlantic joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Air_France%E2%80%93KLM" title="Air France–KLM">Air France–KLM</a> and Alitalia. The program coordinates trans-Atlantic operations, including ticket pricing, schedules, capacity, and revenue. On January 27, 2012, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> launched an investigation into possible violations of <a href="/wiki/Competition_law" title="Competition law">competition law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a> – In 2016, Delta and Korean Air began to lay the groundwork for a trans-Pacific joint venture to compete against those between <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">All Nippon Airways</a>. Unlike other planned joint ventures, the Delta-Korean Air joint venture was quick to receive approval by both the US Department of Transportation and the Korean Ministry of Land, Infrastructure and Transport.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> They aim to increase belly cargo cooperation and offer benefits to its customers across one of the most comprehensive route networks in the trans-Pacific market. This joint venture gives Delta and Korean Air's shared customers seamless access to more than 290 destinations in the Americas and more than 80 in Asia. This joint venture officially launched in May 2018, exactly one year after the joint venture with Aeromexico began.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LATAM_Airlines_Group" title="LATAM Airlines Group">LATAM Airlines Group</a> - In September 2019, Delta announced its plans to buy 20% of LATAM Airlines Group for $1.9 billion which will expand Delta's access to Latin America. In related transactions, Delta is paying to withdraw LATAM from <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">oneworld</a> and also acquired the undelivered <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350 XWB</a> aircraft from the LATAM order book along with two aircraft leased externally by LATAM.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The acquisition of the stake was completed on December 30, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> – On December 11, 2012, Delta announced that it would acquire the 49% stake in Virgin Atlantic held by <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> for $360 million. The two airlines operate a total of 31 roundtrip flights between the UK and North America, including nine daily roundtrip flights between <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow">London</a> and New York City airports (John F. Kennedy International Airport and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a>), with costs shared between the two airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The two airlines' application for antitrust immunity was granted by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">United States Department of Transportation</a> on September 23, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a> – In 2017, Delta announced a joint venture with Virgin Australia, strengthening its trans-Pacific network and allowing the carrier to add direct flights between Australia and the United States.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WestJet" title="WestJet">WestJet</a> – Delta Air Lines and Canadian airline WestJet operate a codeshare agreement on select routes in North America. On July 19, 2018, WestJet and Delta Air Lines signed a ten-year agreement. The airlines' also aligned their frequent flier programs and are co-located at key hub airports.</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:N647DL-2008-08-15-YVR.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/N647DL-2008-08-15-YVR.jpg/220px-N647DL-2008-08-15-YVR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/N647DL-2008-08-15-YVR.jpg/220px-N647DL-2008-08-15-YVR.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:N647DL-2008-08-15-YVR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Delta Air Lines has the largest Boeing 757 fleet of any airline.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Delta_Airlines_-_Boeing_767-300_-_N185DN_(Quintin_Soloviev).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Delta_Airlines_-_Boeing_767-300_-_N185DN_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/220px-Delta_Airlines_-_Boeing_767-300_-_N185DN_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5103" data-file-height="3402"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Delta_Airlines_-_Boeing_767-300_-_N185DN_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/220px-Delta_Airlines_-_Boeing_767-300_-_N185DN_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Delta_Airlines_-_Boeing_767-300_-_N185DN_(Quintin_Soloviev).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Delta Air Lines <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>-300ER at <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines_fleet" title="Delta Air Lines fleet">Delta Air Lines fleet</a></div>
<p>As of March 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delta_Air_Lines&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Delta operates a fleet of 913 aircraft<sup id="cite_ref-Planespotters-Delta_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Planespotters-Delta-6">[6]</a></sup> manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-statsfacts_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsfacts-12">[12]</a></sup> Delta operates the largest <a href="/wiki/Boeing_717" title="Boeing 717">Boeing 717</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-88" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-88">McDonnell Douglas MD-88</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-90" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-90">McDonnell Douglas MD-90</a> fleets in the world, and the largest <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> fleet of any US airline. Prior to its 2008 merger with Northwest Airlines, Delta's fleet was made up of solely Boeing and McDonnell Douglas aircraft. Airbus aircraft from Northwest joined the fleet after the merger, and more have since been added.
</p><p>Delta often seeks to acquire and utilize older aircraft, especially narrow-bodies, and it has created an extensive MRO (maintenance, repair, and overhaul) organization, called TechOps, to support them. The oldest aircraft in the fleet are the McDonnell Douglas MD-88s, with an average age of over 25 years.<sup id="cite_ref-fleetsize_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fleetsize-61">[61]</a></sup> However, in early 2011, Delta began talks with Airbus, Boeing and <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier Aerospace</a> to discuss replacing the McDonnell Douglas DC-9s, MD-88s, and older <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">A320</a> and <a href="/wiki/757-200" class="mw-redirect" title="757-200">757-200</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> On August 22, 2011, Delta placed an order for 100 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-900ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-900ER">Boeing 737-900ER</a> aircraft<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and deferred an order of 100 small narrow-body jets until 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>As part of its strategy to operate less-expensive used airplanes, Delta agreed in 2012 to lease 88 Boeing 717s acquired by <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Airlines" title="Southwest Airlines">Southwest Airlines</a> as part of its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/AirTran_Airways" title="AirTran Airways">AirTran Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> They replaced some DC-9s and some 50-seat regional aircraft such as the <a href="/wiki/CRJ-200" class="mw-redirect" title="CRJ-200">CRJ-200</a>. The first revenue flight was on October 25, 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Delta officially retired its last DC-9 on January 6, 2014; it was used on an as-needed basis until January 22, 2014, when the last one was removed from service.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Delta was the final US carrier operating the DC-9.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> As a continuation of the narrowbody fleet refresh and expansion, Delta ordered 75, and later expanded that order to 95, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A220" title="Airbus A220">Airbus A220</a> (formerly the Bombardier CSeries) aircraft, and became the first American carrier to order the plane.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>The airline has not been as keen to acquire or operate aging wide-body aircraft. In August 2014, Delta announced it would begin to retire its aging <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> fleet, which Delta acquired as part of the Northwest merger.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> During a 2014 earnings call, CEO <a href="/wiki/Richard_H._Anderson_(businessman)" title="Richard H. Anderson (businessman)">Richard Anderson</a> announced that they would be retired by the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> On November 20, 2014, the airline announced an order for 25 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350 XWB</a> and 25 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330neo" title="Airbus A330neo">Airbus A330neo</a> aircraft to replace the 747 fleet as it was retired, as well as some aging 767s. A350 deliveries began in the second quarter of 2017, while the first A330-900neo flew in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Delta retired the 747 on January 3, 2018, with its final revenue flight from Seoul-Incheon to Detroit (DL158) occurring on December 19, 2017, becoming the last major U.S. airline to fly the 747.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>On December 14, 2017, Delta ordered 100 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321neo" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A321neo">Airbus A321neos</a>, with 100 further options for $25.4 billion at list prices, to be delivered from 2020; equipped with <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney">Pratt &amp; Whitney</a> <a href="/wiki/PW1100G" class="mw-redirect" title="PW1100G">PW1100Gs</a> and configured with a maximum capacity of 197 passengers, they will replace the airline's aging <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319s</a>, Airbus A320s, Boeing 757-200s, MD-88s and MD-90s.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabin">Cabin</span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>Delta underwent a cabin branding upgrade in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-CabinRefresh_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabinRefresh-78">[78]</a></sup> The airline now offers or plans to offer six different cabin service options: Delta One, Delta Premium Select, First Class, Comfort+, Main Cabin, and Basic Economy. Availability and exact details vary by route and aircraft type.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Delta_One">Delta One</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Delta_One_Suites_(41341308490).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Delta_One_Suites_%2841341308490%29.jpg/220px-Delta_One_Suites_%2841341308490%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="7957" data-file-height="5305"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Delta_One_Suites_%2841341308490%29.jpg/220px-Delta_One_Suites_%2841341308490%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Delta_One_Suites_(41341308490).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Delta One Suite on a Boeing 777</div></div></div>
<p>Delta One is the airline's premier <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">business class</a> product, available on long haul international flights, as well as <a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_flight" title="Transcontinental flight">transcontinental</a> service from <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York JFK</a> to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_International_Airport" title="San Francisco International Airport">San Francisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seattle%E2%80%93Tacoma_International_Airport" title="Seattle–Tacoma International Airport">Seattle/Tacoma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CabinRefresh_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabinRefresh-78">[78]</a></sup></p><p>Delta One features lie-flat seating on all aircraft types, and direct aisle access from every seat on all types except the Boeing 757-200 (in which only a special sub-fleet of approximately 20 aircraft feature lie-flats).<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-300ER">Boeing 767-300ER</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-400ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-400ER">Boeing 767-400ER</a> seats, designed by <a href="/wiki/James_Thompson_(researcher)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Thompson (researcher)">James Thompson</a>, feature a space-saving design whereby the seats are staggered such that when in the fully flat position, the foot of each bed extends under the armrests of the seat in front of it. Delta One cabins on the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200ER">Boeing 777-200ER</a>/<a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200LR" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200LR">LR</a> fleet are configured in a <a href="/wiki/Herringbone_seating" title="Herringbone seating">herringbone</a> layout, while Airbus A330 cabins (featuring the <i>Cirrus</i> flat-bed sleeper suite by <a href="/wiki/Zodiac_Seats_U.S." class="mw-redirect" title="Zodiac Seats U.S.">Zodiac Seats U.S.</a>) are configured in a reverse herringbone pattern.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>All seats are also equipped with a personal, on demand in-flight-entertainment (IFE) system, universal power-ports, a movable reading light, and a folding work table. Passengers also receive complimentary chef-curated meals, refreshments, alcoholic beverages, a <a href="/wiki/Tumi_Inc." title="Tumi Inc.">Tumi Inc.</a> amenity kit, premium bedding, and pre-flight Sky Club access.<sup id="cite_ref-CabinDetails_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabinDetails-81">[81]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2016, Delta announced the introduction of Delta One Suites on select widebody fleets. The suites will feature a door to the aisle for enhanced privacy, as well as improved storage space, a larger IFE screen, and updated design. The suites will roll out on the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350</a> fleet, first delivered in July 2017, followed by installation within the Boeing 777 fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Premium_Select">Premium Select</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A350-_Interior_-_Premium_Select_(37095459120).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/A350-_Interior_-_Premium_Select_%2837095459120%29.jpg/220px-A350-_Interior_-_Premium_Select_%2837095459120%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2160"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 116px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/A350-_Interior_-_Premium_Select_%2837095459120%29.jpg/220px-A350-_Interior_-_Premium_Select_%2837095459120%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="116" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A350-_Interior_-_Premium_Select_(37095459120).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Delta Premium Select on an Airbus A350-900</div></div></div>
<p>In April 2016, Delta CEO Ed Bastian announced that a new Premium Economy cabin will be added. Since renamed to Premium Select, this cabin will feature extra legroom; adjustable leg rests; extra seat pitch, width, and recline; and a new premium service. Delta introduced it on its new <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350">Airbus A350</a>, first delivered in fall 2017, to be followed by the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In October 2018, Delta announced that they would be selling First Class seats on domestically configured Boeing 757 aircraft flying transatlantic routes as <b>Premium Select</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Class">First Class</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A220_First_Class_(44703804685).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/A220_First_Class_%2844703804685%29.jpg/220px-A220_First_Class_%2844703804685%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="8256" data-file-height="5504"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/A220_First_Class_%2844703804685%29.jpg/220px-A220_First_Class_%2844703804685%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A220_First_Class_(44703804685).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First class on a Delta A220-100</div></div></div>
<p>First Class is offered on mainline domestic flights (except those featuring Delta One service), select short- and medium-haul international flights, and Delta Connection aircraft with more than 50 seats. Seats range from 18.5 to 20.75 inches (47.0 to 52.7 cm) wide and have between 37 and 40 inches (94 and 102 cm) of pitch. Passengers in this class receive a wider variety of free snacks compared to Main Cabin, as well as free drinks and alcohol, and full meal service on flights 900 miles (1,400 km) and longer. Certain aircraft also feature power ports at each seat and free entertainment products from Delta Studio. First Class passengers are also eligible for priority boarding.<sup id="cite_ref-CabinDetails_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabinDetails-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Delta_Comfort.2B"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Delta_Comfort+">Delta Comfort+</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_Delta_Air_Lines_Airbus_A321.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Interior_of_Delta_Air_Lines_Airbus_A321.jpg/220px-Interior_of_Delta_Air_Lines_Airbus_A321.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Interior_of_Delta_Air_Lines_Airbus_A321.jpg/220px-Interior_of_Delta_Air_Lines_Airbus_A321.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_Delta_Air_Lines_Airbus_A321.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Delta Comfort+ on an Airbus A321</div></div></div>
<p>Delta Comfort+ seats are installed on all aircraft excluding Delta's new A350s and feature 34–36 inches (860–910 mm) of pitch; on all Delta One configured aircraft, 35–36 inches (890–910 mm) of pitch and 50 percent more recline over standard Main Cabin seats.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Additional amenities include: Sky Priority Boarding, dedicated overhead space, complimentary beer, wine, and spirits on flights 250 miles (400 km) or more, and complimentary premium snacks on flights 900 miles (1,400 km) or more. Complimentary premium entertainment is available via Delta Studio, with free headsets available on most flights.<sup id="cite_ref-CabinDetails_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabinDetails-81">[81]</a></sup> On transcontinental flights between JFK-LAX/SFO, Delta Comfort+ passengers also get <a href="/wiki/Luvo_Inc." title="Luvo Inc.">Luvo</a> snack wraps. Medallion members can upgrade from Main Cabin to Comfort+ for free, while other customers can upgrade for a fee or with SkyMiles.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_Cabin">Main Cabin</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A350-_Interior_-_Main_Cabin_(23645006548).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/A350-_Interior_-_Main_Cabin_%2823645006548%29.jpg/220px-A350-_Interior_-_Main_Cabin_%2823645006548%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/A350-_Interior_-_Main_Cabin_%2823645006548%29.jpg/220px-A350-_Interior_-_Main_Cabin_%2823645006548%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A350-_Interior_-_Main_Cabin_(23645006548).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Cabin on an Airbus A350-900</div></div></div>
<p>Main Cabin (Economy Class) is available on all aircraft with seats ranging from 17 to 18 inches (43 to 46 cm) wide and 30 to 33 inches (76 to 84 cm) of pitch. The main cabin on Boeing 737, 777, and selected Boeing 757-200, 767-300, and McDonnell Douglas MD-90 aircraft have an articulating seat bottom where the seat bottom moves forward in addition to the seat back tilting backwards when reclining.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-88">[88]</a></sup></p><p>Main Cabin passengers receive complimentary snacks and non-alcoholic drinks on all flights 250 miles (400 km) or longer. Alcoholic beverages are also available for purchase. Complimentary meals and alcoholic drinks are provided on long-haul international flights as well as selected transcontinental domestic flights, such as between New York–JFK and Seattle, San Francisco, Los Angeles, and San Diego.<sup id="cite_ref-delta.com-main-cabin-features_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delta.com-main-cabin-features-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> As part of Delta's Flight Fuel <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> program, meals are available for purchase on other North American flights 900 miles (1,400 km) or longer.<sup id="cite_ref-delta.com-main-cabin-features_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delta.com-main-cabin-features-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>Delta operated a different buy on board program between 2003 and 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The previous program had items from differing providers, depending on the origin and destination of the flight.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Prices ranged up to $10 ($13.54 when adjusted for inflation). The airline started the service on a few selected flights in July 2003, and the meal service was initially offered on 400 flights.<sup id="cite_ref-WeberFreefoodagain_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeberFreefoodagain-95">[95]</a></sup> Delta ended this buy on board program in 2005; instead, Delta began offering snacks at no extra charge on flights over 90 minutes to most U.S. domestic flights and some flights to the Caribbean and Latin America. Beginning in mid-March 2005 the airline planned to stop providing pillows on flights within the 48 contiguous U.S. states, Bermuda, Canada, the Caribbean, and Central America. In addition, the airline increased the price of alcoholic beverages on Delta mainline flights from $4 ($5.24 when adjusted for inflation) to $5 ($6.55 when adjusted for inflation); the increase in alcohol prices did not occur on Song flights.<sup id="cite_ref-WeberFreefoodagain_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeberFreefoodagain-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_Economy">Basic Economy</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Basic_Economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic Economy">Basic Economy</a> is a basic version of Main Cabin, offering the same services with fewer flexibility options for a lower price.<sup id="cite_ref-CabinRefresh_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabinRefresh-78">[78]</a></sup> Examples of fewer flexibility options include no ticket changes, no paid or complimentary upgrades regardless of frequent-flier status, and only having a seat assigned at check-in.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="On-board_amenities">On-board amenities</span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</span></h3>
<p>On August 5, 2008, Delta announced it would be installing the <a href="/wiki/Aircell" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircell">Aircell</a> mobile broadband network, <a href="/wiki/Gogo_Inflight_Internet" title="Gogo Inflight Internet">Gogo Inflight Internet</a>, which enables customers traveling with <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> enabled devices, such as laptops, smartphones, and tablets, to access the Internet for a fee. Gogo was initially offered on Delta's fleet of McDonnell Douglas MD-88 and MD-90 aircraft but has expanded to the remaining domestic fleet, as well as Delta Connection aircraft with a first class cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p><p>Delta has the largest fleet of Wi-Fi equipped aircraft in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The airline introduced its first inflight Wi-Fi on international routes to Tokyo from Los Angeles and Atlanta in March 2014, and stated its intent to offer the service on all transoceanic flight routes by the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Even though Delta had announced the retirement of its 747 fleet, all Delta 747s were Wi-Fi equipped before their withdrawal. Delta is currently installing Wi-Fi on the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777</a> fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>In 2019, the company announced plans to eventually offer free Wi-Fi on all flights.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="In-flight_entertainment">In-flight entertainment</span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span></h4>
<p>In the 1960s, audio programming was introduced where passengers wore headphones consisting of hollow tubes piping in music. These were installed in some Delta aircraft. Some early wide-bodied aircraft, including the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-1011" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed L-1011">Lockheed L-1011</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-200#767-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-200">Boeing 767-200</a>, and <a href="/wiki/767-300#767-300" class="mw-redirect" title="767-300">Boeing 767-300</a> fleet, had movies projected onto the cabin bulkhead. Also during the late 1980s and early 1990s, <a href="/wiki/CRT_display" class="mw-redirect" title="CRT display">CRT</a> monitors over the aisles were added to the 757 fleet, making them the first narrowbody aircraft to feature video entertainment. The MD-90 introduced Delta's first <a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">IFE system</a> with <a href="/wiki/Liquid_crystal_display" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid crystal display">LCD</a> monitors in 1995, and the 777 introduced Delta's first in-seat video system in 1999, initially using the <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_Collins" title="Rockwell Collins">Rockwell Collins</a> Total Entertainment System. Delta's first all-digital IFE system with AVOD (Panasonic eFX) was first introduced in 2003 on Delta's former low-cost subsidiary, Song. The Rockwell Collins IFE system on the 777s was replaced by the Panasonic eFX system in 2007, followed by the Panasonic eX2 in 2011. The Panasonic eFX and eX2 systems are trademarked by Delta as "Delta on Demand".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>In the spring of 2010, Delta installed the Panasonic eFX AVOD system in Economy on six 767-300ERs that are used on routes that are 12 hours or longer.<sup id="cite_ref-flyertalk.com_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flyertalk.com-104">[104]</a></sup> Delta also announced it would be installing AVOD in Economy class on all Boeing 767-300ER and 747 aircraft over the next 3 years.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p><p>On July 27, 2010, Delta announced that it would be the launch customer of the new eX2 AVOD system with the Eco 9i Integrated Smart Monitor, a new ultra-lightweight IFE system by Panasonic Avionics Corporation and <a href="/wiki/Zodiac_Seats_U.S." class="mw-redirect" title="Zodiac Seats U.S.">Zodiac Seats U.S.</a><sup id="cite_ref-panasonic_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panasonic-106">[106]</a></sup> The systems have been installed on the entire 747-400 fleet as of October 2012, and are currently being installed on the 767-300ER fleet (except for the six aircraft previously retrofitted with the eFX system in 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-ifec_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ifec-107">[107]</a></sup> A different version of the Integrated Smart Monitor developed by Panasonic Avionics Corporation and <a href="/wiki/BE_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="BE Aerospace">BE Aerospace</a> was installed on the Airbus A330 fleet. These seats were also installed on all Boeing 757-300, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation#737-900ER" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-900ER</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> and select Boeing 757-200 domestic aircraft, and replaced the existing seats and monitors on the international Boeing 757-200 fleet. The previous seats on the <a href="/wiki/International_flight" title="International flight">international</a> 757-200 fleet have been placed on select <a href="/wiki/Domestic_flight" title="Domestic flight">domestic</a> 757-200 aircraft, mainly ones flying between Hawaii and the U.S. mainland.
</p><p>In 2012, Delta began replacing the overhead CRT monitors on the pre-merger Delta 757-200 fleet with new LCD monitors.<sup id="cite_ref-pvt_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pvt-108">[108]</a></sup> This was completed in late 2012.
</p><p>The 767-400ER fleet initially featured LCDs over the aisles, but were replaced in 2009 by the Panasonic eFX AVOD system when the last of the 767-400ERs were converted from domestic to international use. CRT projectors were originally featured in economy class on <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-300s</a>, with the international 767-300ERs also featuring ceiling-mounted CRT displays over the aisles, which have since replaced by LCD monitors, and are now in the process of being converted to the eFX2 AVOD system.
</p><p>When Delta's ex-<a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">TWA</a> <a href="/wiki/ETOPS" title="ETOPS">ETOPS</a> 757s were first delivered, they featured a system made by Sony Transcom (a former subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> now sold to <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_Collins" title="Rockwell Collins">Rockwell Collins</a>) system that was factory installed for TWA. The system featured overhead drop-down <a href="/wiki/LCD" class="mw-redirect" title="LCD">LCD</a> monitors similar to Delta's non-Transcon 737-800s and 757-300s. Delta replaced the Sony Transcom system with the Panasonic eFX system featuring in-seat video and AVOD at the same time as the new BusinessElite seats and slimline economy class seats were installed.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_fleet">Current fleet</span></h4>
<p>Audio and video are available on all aircraft except for the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-80" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-80">MD-88</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_717" title="Boeing 717">Boeing 717</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-90" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-90">MD-90</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Connection" title="Delta Connection">Delta Connection</a> aircraft. <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200ER">Boeing 777-200ER</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200LR" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200LR">777-200LR</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767#767-300" title="Boeing 767">767-300</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">A330</a> aircraft that have completed cabin modifications, feature the Panasonic eX2 system. Compared to the older eFX system, this offers greater storage capacity, as well as lighter and larger personal video screens.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767#767-400ER" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-400ER</a> aircraft, selected <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757#757-200" title="Boeing 757">757-200</a> aircraft, as well as the remaining internationally configured <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-300ER#767-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-300ER">Boeing 767-300ER</a> aircraft that have not completed cabin modifications, use the <a href="/wiki/Panasonic_Avionics_Corporation" title="Panasonic Avionics Corporation">Panasonic</a> eFX AVOD system.
</p><p>Domestic <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767#767-300" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-300s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation#737-700" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-700s</a>, as well as selected <a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_flight" title="Transcontinental flight">transcontinental</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757#757-200" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757-200s</a> and selected <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation#737-800" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800s</a> using the Panasonic eFX system, also feature live television via <a href="/wiki/Dish_Network" title="Dish Network">Dish Network</a> in both first class and economy. Some <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation#737-800" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800s</a>, as well as all <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757#757-300" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757-300s</a> feature systems with drop-down LCD displays below the overhead bins.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>All aircraft with AVOD, except for the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A220" title="Airbus A220">A220 (formerly CSeries)</a>, feature Panasonic's iXplor moving map program. 737-800s with overhead video and the coach sections of 767-300ER aircraft with overhead video feature the <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_Collins" title="Rockwell Collins">Rockwell Collins</a> Airshow moving map, which is often shown during takeoff and landing. Other aircraft formerly equipped with the Rockwell Collins Airshow moving map included the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-1011_TriStar" title="Lockheed L-1011 TriStar">Lockheed L-1011</a>-250 and -500, <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">MD-11</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767#767-400ER" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-400ER</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">777-200ER</a>. The L-1011 and MD-11 fleet have since been retired, while the 767-400ER and 777-200ER have since had their Airshow systems replaced by the Panasonic iXplor system built into the eFX and eX2 AVOD systems.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Delta_Sky_Magazine">Delta Sky Magazine</span></h3>
<p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.deltaskymag.com">Delta Sky Magazine</a> and its online edition is an airline magazine published by MSP Communications in Minneapolis, Minnesota. It is available in every seat on all routes.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Reward_programs">Reward programs</span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="SkyMiles">SkyMiles</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/SkyMiles" title="SkyMiles">SkyMiles</a></div>
<p>SkyMiles is the <a href="/wiki/Frequent_flyer_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Frequent flyer program">frequent flyer program</a> for Delta Air Lines. Miles do not expire but accounts may be deactivated by Delta in certain cases, such as the death of a program member or fraudulent activity.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Delta_Sky_Club">Delta Sky Club</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Delta_Sky_Club_(29840678206).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/New_Delta_Sky_Club_%2829840678206%29.jpg/220px-New_Delta_Sky_Club_%2829840678206%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/New_Delta_Sky_Club_%2829840678206%29.jpg/220px-New_Delta_Sky_Club_%2829840678206%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Delta_Sky_Club_(29840678206).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A SkyClub in Concourse B at <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p>Delta Sky Club is the branding name of Delta's airport lounges. Membership is available through an annual membership that can be purchased with either money or miles. International passengers traveling in Delta One class get free access. Membership can also be granted through top level Delta status or by being an American Express card holder with certain exceptions. As of January, 2019, Delta no longer offers single day passes.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>Features vary by location, but generally include free drinks (including alcoholic beverages), snacks, and reading material. Wi-Fi is free for members and guests and is mostly provided in the US by AT&amp;T.
</p><p>Originally, Delta's membership-based airport clubs were called Crown Room lounges, with Northwest's called WorldClubs.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="SkyBonus">SkyBonus</span></h3>
<p>On November 27, 2001, Delta Air Lines launched SkyBonus,<sup id="cite_ref-skybonus_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skybonus-115">[115]</a></sup> a program aimed toward small-to-medium businesses spending between $5,000 and $500,000 annually on air travel.<sup id="cite_ref-bonus_press_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bonus_press-116">[116]</a></sup> Businesses can earn points toward free travel and upgrades, as well as Sky Club memberships and SkyMiles Silver Medallion status. Points are earned on paid travel based on a variety of fare amount paid, booking code, and place origin or destination.<sup id="cite_ref-faq_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faq-117">[117]</a></sup> While enrolled businesses are able to earn points toward free travel, the travelling passenger is still eligible to earn SkyMiles during his or her travel.<sup id="cite_ref-faq_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faq-117">[117]</a></sup></p><p>In early 2010, Delta Air Lines merged its SkyBonus program with Northwest's similar Biz Perks program.<sup id="cite_ref-faq_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faq-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span></h3>
<p>For the fiscal year 2018, Delta Air Lines reported earnings of US$5.1 billion, with an annual revenue of US$44.438 billion, an increase of 8.02% over the previous fiscal cycle. Its shares traded at over $48 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$39.182 billion in April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
